## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: The task models the rate of concentration change dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t, which is the fundamental problem in chemical reaction kinetics — determining the rate law. Most rate laws express dA/dt as a function of A alone, but time-dependent forcing or sequential mechanisms can introduce explicit time dependence.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate dependence)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (saturation kinetics, pseudo-Michaelis-Menten)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reactions with equilibrium)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (product-catalyzed, logistic-type kinetics)
- Second-order with equilibrium: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2 (quadratic polynomial rate law)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition at high concentration)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (A**c1 + c2) (Hill-type cooperative rate law)
- Time-modulated first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (rate constant changing exponentially with time)
- Fractional-order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 * A (sum of fractional and first-order terms)
- Consecutive/parallel pathway: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second-order pathways)
- Power-law with time dependence: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (dispersive kinetics in heterogeneous systems)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure concentration dependence (no explicit t) → classical autonomous rate law dA/dt = f(A), typical of well-mixed homogeneous reactions
- Integer power of A → elementary reaction step with molecularity equal to the power (1=unimolecular, 2=bimolecular)
- Non-integer power of A → apparent/effective rate law from complex mechanism or heterogeneous kinetics
- Polynomial in A with multiple terms → competing parallel reaction pathways or reversible reactions
- Rational function of A (denominator with A terms) → enzyme-like or surface-catalyzed mechanism with intermediate saturation
- Product A*(c-A) structure → autocatalytic or logistic mechanism where product accelerates consumption
- Explicit time dependence in rate → non-stationary conditions such as temperature ramp, photochemical forcing, or dispersive kinetics
- Sign of leading coefficient indicates consumption (negative) vs. production (positive) of species A

**Candidate 69:** `A^2*c0 + A*c1 + c2 + c3*sqrt(A+1) + c4*cos(c5*log(A*c6+1))`
Set c1=0, c2=0, c3=0: `A^2*c0 + c4*cos(c5*log(A*c6+1))`. With c5=1, c6=1: `c0*A^2 + c4*cos(log(A+1))`. But GT has sin, not cos. However, `cos(log(A+1)) = sin(log(A+1) + π/2)`. So this is `c4*sin(log(A+1) + π/2)` which equals `c4*cos(log(A+1))`. The GT needs `sin(log(A+1))`, not `cos(log(A+1))`. These are different functions. But wait - can we use the phase? `c4*cos(c5*log(A*c6+1))` - if we allow c5 to be different from 1, then `cos(c5*log(A+1))` ≠ `sin(log(A+1))` for arbitrary c5. Actually, `sin(x) = cos(x - π/2)`, so `sin(log(A+1)) = cos(log(A+1) - π/2)`. But `cos(c5*log(A*c6+1))` requires c5=1 and then it's `cos(log(A+1))`, which has a fixed phase offset of π/2 from sin. We can't add a phase shift to the argument of cos here since there's no additive constant inside the cos. So this is `cos(log(A+1))` ≠ `sin(log(A+1))`.
Candidate 69 verdict: [NO MATCH]

GT: `-c0*A^c1 + c2*_t*sin(log(A + c3))` with `_t=3.379845758334442`. So `_t` is a constant, and the numerical expression is `-0.17495597*A^2 + 0.59132419*sin(log(A+1))`. The GT doesn't actually depend on `t` as a variable - `_t` is a fixed constant.

So for Candidate 73: `A^c2*c3*t^c4` - if we set c3=0, this term vanishes. Then set c1=0, c5=0: `A^2*c0 + c6*sin(...)`. Matches! ✓
